                    <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><div class="player-page-rotowire"><strong><a href="https://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=9266">RotoWire News</a>:</strong> Gonzalez officially re-signed with Colorado on Friday, Jon Heyman of FanRag Sports reports.                 <tr><td><hr class="player-page-info-sep"/><table class="player-page-news"><tr>

                    <td>12/20/2017</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="rg badge">RG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/four-players-with-volatile-2018-outlooks/">Four Players with Volatile 2018 Outlooks</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=88864">Alex Chamberlain</a></span></td></tr><tr>
                    <td>9/14/2017</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="rg badge">RG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/the-sleeper-and-the-bust-episode-496-mike-zunino-batting-champion/">The Sleeper and the Bust Episode: 496  Mike Zunin&#8230;</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=11752">Paul Sporer</a></span></td></tr><tr>
                    <td>8/7/2017</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="fg badge">FG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/the-collapse-of-carlos-gonzalez/">The Collapse of Carlos Gonzalez</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/blogs/index.php?author=20190">Paul Swydan</a></span></td></tr></table></div></td></tr>
            
            </table>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
        
        <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b>The 2009 season was the year that saw Gonzalez begin to turn his projection into production. The minor league version (.290/.348/.484 with 54 stolen bases in 634 games) has still far out-played the Major League version in most categories (.262/.313/.440 with 20 stolen bases in 174 games), but Gonzalez made major strides with increased playing time in 2009. He more than doubled his Major League walk rate (to 9.2%, 7.3% minor league career), cut his reach rate (down to 30.6%), and cut his strikeout rate to 25.2% (21.1% minor league career). He hit more fly balls (up to 38.8%), of which a good percentage left the yard (16.7%), and flashed his wheels on the base paths (16 SBs, 4 CS). He even hit line drives in bunches (23.4%). If he can continue his progression by making more contact next year, this intriguing power/speed prospect could solidify his star status.<br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b>The second half of last year saw nothing but Go CarGo, as Gonzalez hit .320/.384/.608 with 12 home runs and 11 stolen bases and established himself as a starting outfielder and fantasy sleeper extraordinaire in 2010. You could try to poo-poo the exciting young player's sleeper credentials by talking about how crowded the outfield is, or how CarGo still strikes out too much to be counted on for a good batting average. But the fact is, with his great defense (+12.8 UZR/150 in center), he'll get the chance to right any short slumps next year, even if he starts out poorly. So you are left with a player with serious wheels, nice pop, great defense, and star quality on a team mostly devoid of flashy young players. If Gonzalez continues to steal at his Major League pace, Grady Sizemore Part Two is not out of the realm of possibilities here.  (Eno Sarris)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Always viewed as a potential five tool player, the breakout came in a big way in 2010.  Gonzalez made a run at the triple crown while also stealing 26 bases, making him among the very best performers in almost any fantasy scoring system.  That said, you probably shouldnt expect a repeat, and youll want to include a lot of room for regression in your valuation.  Gonzalezs strikeout rate is simply too high to support a .336 average, even for a player who spends half his games in Colorado.  With a drop in his BABIP essentially inevitable, his average will fall, and with fewer opportunities on the bases, his stolen base totals could decline as well.  While he may look like a 30-30 player in the making, you should draft Gonzalez mostly for the power numbers and let everything else be a bonus.  The overall package is still tremendously valuable, but dont expect him to be Hanley Ramirez.  (Dave Cameron)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>A candidate to take a big step back in 2011.  You probably don't want to pay what the going rate for him will be, as 2010 will inflate expectations that he probably can't live up to.  </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>After a fantasy MVP type season in 2010, Gonzalez came back to earth a little in 2011. He still looks to be one of the top fantasy players in the game with 20-20 skills and a .300 average most years. People should have expected some regression in his 2011 average from 2010 when he had a .384 batting average on balls in play. His BABIP dropped to .326 and his average went to .295. The biggest hit to his value came from an early July wrist injury. Because of it, he played in 18 fewer games than in 2010. He was on pace for 30+ home runs and 110 runs and 110 RBI. The biggest knock against him is his home (.329/.381/.609) vs away splits (.265/.317/.427). Even with this split, he will again find himself at the top of the fantasy rankings. I see no reason he should not be drafted in the first or second round in 2012. (Jeff Zimmerman)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Cargo is a great fantasy option with his only flaw being a huge home and away split.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>For the second straight season, CarGo battled through some nagging injuries that may have hampered his performance at the plate. Still, he managed to reward fantasy owners as usual with his exciting power and speed skills. One major concern for Gonzalez is his declining fly ball rate. Obviously, as a power hitter who calls Coors Field home, the more fly balls, the better. If he were to return to the 30 home run plateau, he would need to lift the ball on a more frequent basis. If he does manage to stay healthy, then his 2010 performance, minus the batting average, could happen again. As a result, he's one of the few top-tier hitters who you could still potentially earn a profit from. (<a target="_blank" href="http://www.pallocale.com/">Mike Podhorzer</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Despite missing some time due to various ailments once again, CarGo contributed nicely in all five categories. Although his power has declined a bit, his skills remain strong and at age 27, is right in the middle of his prime.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>CarGo posted his fourth consecutive 20-20 season in 2013 and over that span, he's seen his batting average drop below .300 only once -- .295 in 2011. What's even more impressive is that during his last three seasons, he posted these types of numbers, while failing to play in more than 135 games due to a variety of injuries, including a sprained finger which cost him the final two months of the season last year. A more aggressive approach at the plate in 2013 helped him end a recent power decline but he did see a spike in his strikeout rate, though it didn't seem to have an adverse effect any of his other numbers -- his average and stolen base total remained the same. Moving forward, he'll look to continue his assault on NL pitching and, still in his prime at age-28, should produce yet another first-round worthy season. There is a bit of concern as to how his work at the plate will be affected by his decision not to have surgery on his injured finger, but those concerns should be assuaged with a healthy spring training. (Howard Bender)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>After four consecutive 20-20 seasons, there is little argument against CarGo being a top-10 fantasy pick in 2014. Last season, he took a more aggressive approach at the plate to help stop a recent power slide, and while he saw a spike in his strikeout rate, there were no adverse effects on the rest of his numbers. Spring training will prove his health, his consistent numbers have proven his value.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Nothing is ever easy for Carlos Gonzalez. Making the ball go over the fence is something he's always done well, but Gonzalez is quickly toeing the line between "valuable" and "liability" because he simply can't stay on the field. 2014 was the worst of both worlds for the Rockies outfielder, as he played in a career-low 70 games while putting up the worst numbers of his life -- .238/.292/.431 and 11 home runs and only three steals. His in-play average dipped well below his career norms (.283 BABIP compared to .344 career) but the Rockies outfielder swung more, chased more, and whiffed more while producing less power than in the past. It was the worst case scenario after Gonzalez accepted more strikeouts in exchange for bigger numbers during his 2013 career year --.302/.367/.591 with 26 homers and 21 steals in 436 plate appearances, as you might recall. His rough 2014 might cause some to overlook Gonzalez as an option next year, but his talent is undeniable. Still only 29, CarGo has a lot left to give. Take your medicine and reap the rewards of his skills (and altitude) put make sure to keep an injury replacement in your back pocket. (Drew Fairservice)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>The injury-prone slugger did too much of one (missing time) and not enough of the other (hitting home runs) in 2014, but Carlos Gonzalez is too talented to overlook in 2015.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>There was a time when Carlos Gonzalez was a legitimate star. And if you judge strictly by his home run totals, you would presume that he still is. This is not the case, unfortunately. His batting average and stolen base numbers have dropped drastically. His on-base percentage -- never elite -- has also slipped, along with his walk rate. More troubling however, as detailed by August Fagerstrom in January, is that Gonzalez now has some incredibly troubling platoon splits. With offense that was 67% worse than league average against left-handed pitchers over the last two seasons, it is becoming increasingly clear that Gonzalez needs to be platooned. He may not be though, so this puts the onus on you, the fantasy player, to pay attention to the opposing starting pitcher and adjust accordingly. Gonzalez is still capable of hitting 25 home runs a season, and you could be forgiven if you felt there was still some light left in him. But chances are he is now a player who won't hit for a high average, steal bases or hit well against left-handed pitching. There are certainly worse players to have around, but definitely don't draft Gonzalez to be one of your lineup anchors. (Paul Swydan)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Carlos Gonzalez's power is not yet diminished, but much of the rest of his game is in decline. Don't draft him expecting him to be a star.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Having played consecutive seasons with 600 plate appearances for the first time in his career, Gonzalez looks as healthy as ever. Perhaps it's because he no longer has to patrol Coors' expansive center field, or because he's stopped running. The former is good for fantasy, the latter not so much. After the most impressive power display of his career in 2015, CarGo bucked the trend last year. As homers soared league-wide in 2016, Gonzalez hit 15 fewer homers on his way to the second-worst park-adjusted offense of his career. An unsustainable home run-to-fly ball rate came crashing down, he struggled mightily against lefties, and struggled to tread water on the road. This isn't to say 2016 was all bad. Twenty-five homers still plays, as do 87 runs and 100 RBI. And his .298 batting average proves he retains an excellent hit tool. But without the stolen bases, there's no longer a ton of upside here, and there's a growing health risk as he ages. While delivering positive value across four standard roto categories in 2016, Gonzalez' decline in speed positions him further away from five-category production than ever before. He's also heavily dependent on his home ballpark, and a mid-season trade from Colorado would absolutely sap his value. (Rylan Edwards)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>At 31 years old, Gonzalez remains productive even if he finds it more difficult to conceal his flaws. Ever the streaky player, Gonzalez is an even riskier investment now.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>

        }
        else {
            panelo.style.display = 'none';
            document.getElementById('soa3').style.fontWeight = 'normal';
        }
    }

    function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    function setPart(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_multi' || node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_multi') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }

<script type="text/javascript">
    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Make sure to only match links to wikipedia with a rel tag
        $('a[tipgloss]').each(function () {
            // We make use of the .each() loop to gain access to each element via the "this" keyword...
            $(this).qtip(
		{
		    content: {
		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use
		        text: " ",
		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },
		    hide: {
		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,
		        fixed: true
		    },
		    style: {
		        classes: "qtip-light"
		    }
		})

            // Make sure it doesn't follow the link when we click it
        });
    });
</script>
